There is a simple convert from f16 to fp8 for input vec, however, the dxil looks incorrect.
hlsl:
typedef vector<half, 16> half16;
half16 srcF16 = inbuf.Load<half16>(0);
InterpretedVector<uint, 4, ComponentEnum::F8_E4M3FN> converted =
      Convert<ComponentEnum::F8_E4M3FN, ComponentEnum::F16>(srcF16);

dxil:
  %4 = call %dx.types.ResRet.v16f16 @dx.op.rawBufferVectorLoad.v16f16(i32 303, %dx.types.Handle %3, i32 0, i32 undef, i32 2)  ; RawBufferVectorLoad(buf,index,elementOffset,alignment)
  %5 = extractvalue %dx.types.ResRet.v16f16 %4, 0
  %6 = shufflevector <16 x half> %5, <16 x half> undef, <4 x i32> <i32 0, i32 1, i32 2, i32 3>
  %7 = call <4 x i32> @dx.op.linAlgConvert.v4i32.v4f16(i32 -2147483618, **<4 x half> %6**, i32 8, i32 21)  ; LinAlgConvert(**inputVector**,inputInterpretation,outputInterpretation)

we expected <16 x half> %5 as the convert input, but it shufflevector to <4xhalf> which is not expected.

Is there something wrong from this hlsl or dxc problem

   225	template <ComponentEnum ComponentTy, SIZE_TYPE M, SIZE_TYPE N,

   227	class Matrix {
   228	  using ElementType = typename __detail::ComponentTypeTraits<ComponentTy>::Type;
   229	  // If this isn't a native scalar, we have an 8-bit type, so we have 4 elements
   230	  // packed in each scalar value.

   241	            bool Transpose = false>
   242	  Matrix<NewCompTy, M, N, NewUse, Scope> Cast() {
   243	    Matrix<NewCompTy, M, N, NewUse, Scope> Result;
   244	    __builtin_LinAlg_CopyConvertMatrix(Result.__handle, __handle, Transpose);
   245	    return Result;
   246	  }

   756	// Returns true if pow can be implemented using Fxc's mul-only code gen pattern.
   757	// Fxc uses the below rules when choosing mul-only code gen pattern to implement
   758	// pow function. Rule 1: Applicable only to power values in the range
   759	// [INT32_MIN, INT32_MAX] Rule 2: The maximum number of mul ops needed shouldn't
   760	// exceed (2n+1) or (n+1) based on whether the power
   761	//         is a positive or a negative value. Here "n" is the number of scalar
   762	//         elements in power.
   763	// Rule 3: Power must be an exact value.
   764	// +----------+---------------------+------------------+
   765	// | BaseType | IsExponentPositive  | MaxMulOpsAllowed |
   766	// +----------+---------------------+------------------+
   767	// | float4x4 | True                |               33 |
   768	// | float4x4 | False               |               17 |
   769	// | float4x2 | True                |               17 |
   770	// | float4x2 | False               |                9 |
   771	// | float2x4 | True                |               17 |
   772	// | float2x4 | False               |                9 |
   773	// | float4   | True                |                9 |
   774	// | float4   | False               |                5 |
   775	// | float2   | True                |                5 |
   776	// | float2   | False               |                3 |
   777	// | float    | True                |                3 |
   778	// | float    | False               |                2 |
   779	// +----------+---------------------+------------------+
   780	
   781	bool CanUseFxcMulOnlyPatternForPow(IRBuilder<> &Builder, Value *x, Value *pow,
   782	                                   int32_t &powI) {
   783	  // Applicable only when power is a literal.
   784	  if (!isa<ConstantDataVector>(pow) && !isa<ConstantFP>(pow)) {
   785	    return false;
   786	  }
   787	
   788	  // Only apply this code gen on splat values.
   789	  if (ConstantDataVector *cdv = dyn_cast<ConstantDataVector>(pow)) {
   790	    if (!hlsl::dxilutil::IsSplat(cdv)) {
   791	      return false;
   792	    }
   793	  }
   794	
   795	  // Only apply on aggregates of 16 or fewer elements,
   796	  // representing the max 4x4 matrix size.
   797	  Type *Ty = x->getType();
   798	  if (Ty->isVectorTy() && Ty->getVectorNumElements() > 16)
   799	    return false;

   956	// Tunnel through insert/extract element and shuffle to find original source
   957	// of scalar value, or specified element (vecIdx) of vector value.
   958	Value *FindScalarSource(Value *src, unsigned vecIdx = 0) {
   959	  Type *srcTy = src->getType()->getScalarType();
   960	  while (src && !isa<UndefValue>(src)) {
   961	    if (src->getType()->isVectorTy()) {
   962	      if (InsertElementInst *IE = dyn_cast<InsertElementInst>(src)) {
   963	        unsigned curIdx = (unsigned)cast<ConstantInt>(IE->getOperand(2))
   964	                              ->getUniqueInteger()
   965	                              .getLimitedValue();
   966	        src = IE->getOperand((curIdx == vecIdx) ? 1 : 0);
   967	      } else if (ShuffleVectorInst *SV = dyn_cast<ShuffleVectorInst>(src)) {
   968	        int newIdx = SV->getMaskValue(vecIdx);
   969	        if (newIdx < 0)
   970	          return UndefValue::get(srcTy);
   971	        vecIdx = (unsigned)newIdx;
   972	        src = SV->getOperand(0);
   973	        unsigned numElt = src->getType()->getVectorNumElements();
   974	        if (numElt <= vecIdx) {
   975	          vecIdx -= numElt;
   976	          src = SV->getOperand(1);
   977	        }
   978	      } else {
   979	        return UndefValue::get(srcTy); // Didn't find it.
   980	      }
   981	    } else {
   982	      if (ExtractElementInst *EE = dyn_cast<ExtractElementInst>(src)) {
   983	        vecIdx = (unsigned)cast<ConstantInt>(EE->getIndexOperand())
   984	                     ->getUniqueInteger()
   985	                     .getLimitedValue();
   986	        src = EE->getVectorOperand();
   987	      } else if (hlsl::dxilutil::IsConvergentMarker(src)) {
   988	        src = hlsl::dxilutil::GetConvergentSource(src);
   989	      } else {
   990	        break; // Found it.
   991	      }
   992	    }
   993	  }
   994	  return src;
   995	}

This is not the issue either. Let me think about the problem differently. The PR description says:

```
%6 = shufflevector <16 x half> %5, <16 x half> undef, <4 x i32> <i32 0, i32 1, i32 2, i32 3>
%7 = call <4 x i32> @dx.op.linAlgConvert.v4i32.v4f16(i32 -2147483618, <4 x half> %6, i32 8, i32 21)
```

So the input vector `<16 x half>` is being shuffled to `<4 x half>` before the convert call. But we expect the full `<16 x half>` to be passed. The convert function signature is `<4 x i32> @dx.op.linAlgConvert.v4i32.v4f16` which takes `<4 x half>` and returns `<4 x i32>`. 

The issue seems to be in the translation of the Convert template. Looking at the header:

```cpp
template <ComponentEnum DestTy, ComponentEnum OriginTy, typename T, int N>
InterpretedVector<typename __detail::ComponentTypeTraits<DestTy>::Type,
                  __detail::DstN<DestTy, OriginTy, N>::Value, DestTy>
Convert(vector<T, N> Vec) {
  vector<typename __detail::ComponentTypeTraits<DestTy>::Type,
         __detail::DstN<DestTy, OriginTy, N>::Value>
      Result;
  __builtin_LinAlg_Convert(Result, Vec, OriginTy, DestTy);
  return MakeInterpretedVector<DestTy>(Result);
}
```

So when we call `Convert<ComponentEnum::F8_E4M3FN, ComponentEnum::F16>(srcF16)`:
- `srcF16` is `vector<half, 16>` i.e., `<16 x half>`
- `DestTy` = `F8_E4M3FN`
- `OriginTy` = `F16`
- `T` = `half`
- `N` = 16

For `ComponentTypeTraits<F16>`: `Type = float16_t`, `IsNativeScalar = true`, `ElementsPerScalar = 1`
For `ComponentTypeTraits<F8_E4M3FN>`: `Type = uint`, `IsNativeScalar = false`, `ElementsPerScalar = 4`

So `DstN<F8_E4M3FN, F16, 16>::Value = (16 * 1) / 4 = 4`

So the result type should be `InterpretedVector<uint, 4, F8_E4M3FN>` - meaning a `<4 x uint>` (since fp8 has 4 elements per 32-bit scalar).

The builtin call is `__builtin_LinAlg_Convert(Result, Vec, OriginTy, DestTy)` where:
- Result is `vector<uint, 4>` 
- Vec is `vector<half, 16>`

So the intrinsic should be called with `<16 x half>` as the input vector, not `<4 x half>`. The shufflevector is wrong.

Let me search for how the intrinsic arguments are matched and potentially generate shuffles

  4039	static unsigned GetHLOpcode(const Expr *E) {
  4040	  switch (E->getStmtClass()) {
  4041	  case Stmt::CompoundAssignOperatorClass:
  4042	  case Stmt::BinaryOperatorClass: {
  4043	    const clang::BinaryOperator *binOp = cast<clang::BinaryOperator>(E);
  4044	    HLBinaryOpcode binOpcode = BinaryOperatorKindMap[binOp->getOpcode()];
  4045	    if (HasUnsignedOpcode(binOpcode)) {
  4046	      if (hlsl::IsHLSLUnsigned(binOp->getLHS()->getType())) {
  4047	        binOpcode = GetUnsignedOpcode(binOpcode);
  4048	      }
  4049	    }
  4050	    return static_cast<unsigned>(binOpcode);
  4051	  }
  4052	  case Stmt::UnaryOperatorClass: {
  4053	    const UnaryOperator *unOp = cast<clang::UnaryOperator>(E);
  4054	    HLUnaryOpcode unOpcode = UnaryOperatorKindMap[unOp->getOpcode()];
  4055	    return static_cast<unsigned>(unOpcode);
  4056	  }
  4057	  case Stmt::ImplicitCastExprClass:
  4058	  case Stmt::CStyleCastExprClass: {
  4059	    const CastExpr *CE = cast<CastExpr>(E);
  4060	    bool toUnsigned = hlsl::IsHLSLUnsigned(E->getType());
  4061	    bool fromUnsigned = hlsl::IsHLSLUnsigned(CE->getSubExpr()->getType());
  4062	    if (toUnsigned && fromUnsigned)
  4063	      return static_cast<unsigned>(HLCastOpcode::UnsignedUnsignedCast);
  4064	    else if (toUnsigned)
  4065	      return static_cast<unsigned>(HLCastOpcode::ToUnsignedCast);
  4066	    else if (fromUnsigned)
  4067	      return static_cast<unsigned>(HLCastOpcode::FromUnsignedCast);
  4068	    else
  4069	      return static_cast<unsigned>(HLCastOpcode::DefaultCast);
  4070	  }
  4071	  default:
  4072	    return 0;
  4073	  }
  4074	}

  4076	static Value *
  4077	EmitHLSLMatrixOperationCallImp(CGBuilderTy &Builder, HLOpcodeGroup group,
  4078	                               unsigned opcode, llvm::Type *RetType,
  4079	                               ArrayRef<Value *> paramList, llvm::Module &M) {
  4080	  SmallVector<llvm::Type *, 4> paramTyList;
  4081	  // Add the opcode param
  4082	  llvm::Type *opcodeTy = llvm::Type::getInt32Ty(M.getContext());
  4083	  paramTyList.emplace_back(opcodeTy);
  4084	  for (Value *param : paramList) {
  4085	    paramTyList.emplace_back(param->getType());
  4086	  }
  4087	
  4088	  llvm::FunctionType *funcTy =
  4089	      llvm::FunctionType::get(RetType, paramTyList, false);
  4090	
  4091	  Function *opFunc = GetOrCreateHLFunction(M, funcTy, group, opcode);
  4092	
  4093	  SmallVector<Value *, 4> opcodeParamList;
  4094	  Value *opcodeConst = Constant::getIntegerValue(opcodeTy, APInt(32, opcode));
  4095	  opcodeParamList.emplace_back(opcodeConst);
  4096	  opcodeParamList.append(paramList.begin(), paramList.end());
  4097	
  4098	  return Builder.CreateCall(opFunc, opcodeParamList);
  4099	}

Now, the Convert function template:

```cpp
template <ComponentEnum DestTy, ComponentEnum OriginTy, typename T, int N>
InterpretedVector<...>
Convert(vector<T, N> Vec) {
  vector<typename __detail::ComponentTypeTraits<DestTy>::Type,
         __detail::DstN<DestTy, OriginTy, N>::Value>
      Result;
  __builtin_LinAlg_Convert(Result, Vec, OriginTy, DestTy);
  return MakeInterpretedVector<DestTy>(Result);
}
```

When `Convert<ComponentEnum::F8_E4M3FN, ComponentEnum::F16>(srcF16)` is called with `srcF16` being `vector<half, 16>`:
- `DestTy` = `F8_E4M3FN`
- `OriginTy` = `F16`
- `T` = `half` (deduced from argument)
- `N` = 16 (deduced from argument)
- `Result` type = `vector<uint, 4>` (since `DstN<F8_E4M3FN, F16, 16>::Value = 4`)

So the intrinsic call should be:
```
__builtin_LinAlg_Convert(Result, Vec, OriginTy, DestTy)
```
Where:
- `Result` is `vector<uint, 4>&` (output)
- `Vec` is `vector<half, 16>` (input)
- `OriginTy` is `F16` = 8
- `DestTy` is `F8_E4M3FN` = 21

Now, let me look at the intrinsic table definition:

```
AR_QUAL_OUT: ret (LITEMPLATE_ANY, LICOMPTYPE_NUMERIC) 
AR_QUAL_IN: vec (LITEMPLATE_ANY, LICOMPTYPE_NUMERIC)
AR_QUAL_IN: input_interp (LITEMPLATE_SCALAR, LICOMPTYPE_UINT)
AR_QUAL_IN: output_interp (LITEMPLATE_SCALAR, LICOMPTYPE_UINT)
```

The `ret` and `vec` are `LITEMPLATE_ANY` which means they can be any type. The problem might be in how the clang codegen handles the intrinsic call when the input and output vector types have different sizes.

   217	        # Contrived example: "hf<,<fd,i<1"
   218	        #   - "," splits multiple overload dimensions
   219	        #   - In the first overload dimension "hf<":
   220	        #     - "hf" means overloads for scalar half and float
   221	        #     - ending with "<" means vector overload supporting the same
   222	        #       components as defined for the scalar overload types.
   223	        #   - In the second overload dimension "<fd":
   224	        #     - starting with "<" means only vector overloads are supported.
   225	        #     - "fd" means the vector supports float or double components.
   226	        #   - In the third overload dimension "i<1":
   227	        #     - "i" means it supports a scalar i32 overload
   228	        #     - "<1" means it also supports a vector overload with an i1
   229	        #       component type.
   230	        oload_types = self.oload_types.split(",")
   231	        self.num_oloads = len(oload_types)
   232	        if self.num_oloads > dxil_max_overload_dims:
   233	            raise ValueError(
   234	                "Too many overload dimensions for DXIL op "
   235	                f"{self.name}: '{self.oload_types}'"
   236	            )
   237	
   238	        def check_duplicate_overloads(oloads):
   239	            if len(oloads) != len(set(oloads)):
   240	                raise ValueError(
   241	                    "Duplicate overload types specified for DXIL op "
   242	                    f"{self.name}: '{oloads}' in '{self.oload_types}'"
   243	                )
   244	
   245	        def check_overload_chars(oloads, valid_chars):

   248	                raise ValueError(
   249	                    "Invalid overload type character(s) used for DXIL op "
   250	                    f"{self.name}: '{invalid_chars}' in '{oloads}' from "
   251	                    f"'{self.oload_types}'"
   252	                )

So for `LinAlgConvert`:
- Result type: `EXT(0)` (first overload type)
- Opcode: `pI32` (i32)
- Input vector: `EXT(1)` (second overload type)
- Input interpretation: `pI32`
- Output interpretation: `pI32`

So the function signature is determined by two overload types: `EXT(0)` for the result and `EXT(1)` for the input. 

Now let me look at where the function is called - in TranslateLinAlgConvert:

```cpp
Value *TranslateLinAlgConvert(CallInst *CI, ...) {
  ...
  Value *OutVecPtr = CI->getArgOperand(1);
  Type *OutVecTy = OutVecPtr->getType()->getPointerElementType();
  Value *InVec = CI->getArgOperand(2);
  ...
  Function *DxilFunc = HlslOp->GetOpFunc(OpCode, {OutVecTy, InVec->getType()});
  Value *OutVec = Builder.CreateCall(DxilFunc, {OpArg, InVec, InInterp, OutInterp});
  Builder.CreateStore(OutVec, OutVecPtr);
  return nullptr;
}
```

This seems correct - it passes both `OutVecTy` and `InVec->getType()` as the overload types.

But wait, the PR description shows:
```
%6 = shufflevector <16 x half> %5, <16 x half> undef, <4 x i32> <i32 0, i32 1, i32 2, i32 3>
%7 = call <4 x i32> @dx.op.linAlgConvert.v4i32.v4f16(i32 -2147483618, <4 x half> %6, i32 8, i32 21)
```

The function is `v4i32.v4f16` - meaning the result is `<4 x i32>` and the input is `<4 x f16>`. But the original input was `<16 x half>`, not `<4 x half>`. 

So somewhere between the HLSL frontend and this lowering, the input vector was shuffled from `<16 x half>` to `<4 x half>`. Let me trace backwards to find where this happens.

The HLSL frontend (clang) generates the intrinsic call. Let me look at how the intrinsic call is generated in CGHLSLMS.cpp

  4101	static Value *EmitHLSLArrayInit(CGBuilderTy &Builder, HLOpcodeGroup group,
  4102	                                unsigned opcode, llvm::Type *RetType,
  4103	                                ArrayRef<Value *> paramList, llvm::Module &M) {
  4104	  // It's a matrix init.
  4105	  if (!RetType->isVoidTy())
  4106	    return EmitHLSLMatrixOperationCallImp(Builder, group, opcode, RetType,
  4107	                                          paramList, M);
  4108	  Value *arrayPtr = paramList[0];
  4109	  llvm::ArrayType *AT =
  4110	      cast<llvm::ArrayType>(arrayPtr->getType()->getPointerElementType());
  4111	  // Avoid the arrayPtr.
  4112	  unsigned paramSize = paramList.size() - 1;
  4113	  // Support simple case here.
  4114	  if (paramSize == AT->getArrayNumElements()) {
  4115	    bool typeMatch = true;
  4116	    llvm::Type *EltTy = AT->getArrayElementType();
  4117	    if (EltTy->isAggregateType()) {
  4118	      // Aggregate Type use pointer in initList.
  4119	      EltTy = llvm::PointerType::get(EltTy, 0);
  4120	    }
  4121	    for (unsigned i = 1; i < paramList.size(); i++) {
  4122	      if (paramList[i]->getType() != EltTy) {
  4123	        typeMatch = false;
  4124	        break;
  4125	      }
  4126	    }
  4127	    // Both size and type match.
  4128	    if (typeMatch) {
  4129	      bool isPtr = EltTy->isPointerTy();
  4130	      llvm::Type *i32Ty = llvm::Type::getInt32Ty(EltTy->getContext());
  4131	      Constant *zero = ConstantInt::get(i32Ty, 0);
  4132	
  4133	      for (unsigned i = 1; i < paramList.size(); i++) {
  4134	        Constant *idx = ConstantInt::get(i32Ty, i - 1);
  4135	        Value *GEP = Builder.CreateInBoundsGEP(arrayPtr, {zero, idx});
  4136	        Value *Elt = paramList[i];
  4137	
  4138	        if (isPtr) {
  4139	          Elt = Builder.CreateLoad(Elt);
  4140	        }
  4141	
  4142	        Builder.CreateStore(Elt, GEP);
  4143	      }
  4144	      // The return value will not be used.
  4145	      return nullptr;
  4146	    }
  4147	  }
  4148	  // Other case will be lowered in later pass.
  4149	  return EmitHLSLMatrixOperationCallImp(Builder, group, opcode, RetType,
  4150	                                        paramList, M);

  7031	      break;
  7032	    default:
  7033	      badArgIdx = std::min(badArgIdx, iArg); // no struct, arrays or void
  7034	    }
  7035	
  7036	    DXASSERT(
  7037	        pIntrinsicArg->uTemplateId < MaxIntrinsicArgs,
  7038	        "otherwise intrinsic table was modified and g_MaxIntrinsicParamCount "
  7039	        "was not updated (or uTemplateId is out of bounds)");
  7040	
  7041	    // Compare template
  7042	    if ((AR_TOBJ_UNKNOWN == Template[pIntrinsicArg->uTemplateId]) ||
  7043	        ((AR_TOBJ_SCALAR == Template[pIntrinsicArg->uTemplateId]) &&
  7044	         (AR_TOBJ_VECTOR == TypeInfoShapeKind ||
  7045	          AR_TOBJ_MATRIX == TypeInfoShapeKind))) {
  7046	      // Unrestricted or truncation of tuples to scalars are allowed
  7047	      Template[pIntrinsicArg->uTemplateId] = TypeInfoShapeKind;
  7048	    } else if (AR_TOBJ_SCALAR == TypeInfoShapeKind) {
  7049	      if (AR_TOBJ_SCALAR != Template[pIntrinsicArg->uTemplateId] &&
  7050	          AR_TOBJ_VECTOR != Template[pIntrinsicArg->uTemplateId] &&
  7051	          AR_TOBJ_MATRIX != Template[pIntrinsicArg->uTemplateId]) {
  7052	        // Scalars to tuples can be splatted, scalar to anything else is not
  7053	        // allowed
  7054	        badArgIdx = std::min(badArgIdx, iArg);
  7055	      }
  7056	    } else {
  7057	      if (TypeInfoShapeKind != Template[pIntrinsicArg->uTemplateId]) {
  7058	        // Outside of simple splats and truncations, templates must match
  7059	        badArgIdx = std::min(badArgIdx, iArg);
  7060	      }

Now I see something interesting. The template matching checks if the shapes match. Both `ret` and `vec` have `uTemplateId = 1` and `2` respectively (from the intrinsic table). Each has its own template slot. 

But I think the issue might not be in Sema but rather in how the function type is constructed and then how the HL operation lowering pass handles it. Let me look at the TranslateLinAlgConvert more carefully and see if the issue is there.

Looking again at the PR description:
```
%4 = call %dx.types.ResRet.v16f16 @dx.op.rawBufferVectorLoad.v16f16(...)
%5 = extractvalue %dx.types.ResRet.v16f16 %4, 0
%6 = shufflevector <16 x half> %5, <16 x half> undef, <4 x i32> <i32 0, i32 1, i32 2, i32 3>
%7 = call <4 x i32> @dx.op.linAlgConvert.v4i32.v4f16(i32 -2147483618, <4 x half> %6, i32 8, i32 21)
```

The input `<16 x half>` is shuffled to `<4 x half>`. So somewhere, the code is creating a shufflevector to truncate the input. This shuffle is NOT in TranslateLinAlgConvert (which is relatively simple). It must be happening before the lowering pass.

Let me look at the HL intrinsic function definition and how it's generated in clang codegen. Specifically, when the Convert function calls `__builtin_LinAlg_Convert(Result, Vec, OriginTy, DestTy)`, the clang codegen needs to generate a call to the intrinsic. But the intrinsic function signature has `ret` and `vec` with potentially different vector sizes.

   641	
   642	Function *GetOrCreateHLFunction(Module &M, FunctionType *funcTy,
   643	                                HLOpcodeGroup group, StringRef *groupName,
   644	                                StringRef *fnName, unsigned opcode,
   645	                                const AttributeSet &origAttribs) {
   646	  // Set/transfer all common attributes
   647	  AttributeSet attribs = GetHLFunctionAttributes(M.getContext(), funcTy,
   648	                                                 origAttribs, group, opcode);
   649	
   650	  std::string mangledName;
   651	  raw_string_ostream mangledNameStr(mangledName);
   652	  if (group == HLOpcodeGroup::HLExtIntrinsic) {
   653	    assert(groupName && "else intrinsic should have been rejected");
   654	    assert(fnName && "else intrinsic should have been rejected");
   655	    mangledNameStr << *groupName;
   656	    mangledNameStr << '.';
   657	    mangledNameStr << *fnName;
   658	    attribs = attribs.addAttribute(M.getContext(), AttributeSet::FunctionIndex,
   659	                                   hlsl::HLPrefix, *groupName);
   660	  } else {
   661	    mangledNameStr << GetHLFullName(group, opcode, attribs);
   662	    mangledNameStr << '.';
   663	    funcTy->print(mangledNameStr);
   664	  }
   665	
   666	  mangledNameStr.flush();
   667	
   668	  // Avoid getOrInsertFunction to verify attributes and type without casting.
   669	  Function *F = cast_or_null<Function>(M.getNamedValue(mangledName));
   670	  if (F) {
   671	    assert(F->getFunctionType() == funcTy &&
   672	           "otherwise, function type mismatch not captured by mangling");
   673	    // Compare attribute mangling to ensure function attributes are as expected.
   674	    assert(
   675	        GetHLFunctionAttributeMangling(F->getAttributes().getFnAttributes()) ==
   676	            GetHLFunctionAttributeMangling(attribs) &&
   677	        "otherwise, function attribute mismatch not captured by mangling");
   678	  } else {
   679	    F = cast<Function>(M.getOrInsertFunction(mangledName, funcTy, attribs));
   680	  }
   681	
   682	  return F;
   683	}
   684	
   685	// HLFunction with body cannot share with HLFunction without body.
   686	// So need add name.
   687	Function *GetOrCreateHLFunctionWithBody(Module &M, FunctionType *funcTy,
   688	                                        HLOpcodeGroup group, unsigned opcode,
   689	                                        StringRef name) {
   690	  // Set/transfer all common attributes
   691	  AttributeSet attribs = GetHLFunctionAttributes(M.getContext(), funcTy,
   692	                                                 AttributeSet(), group, opcode);
   693	
   694	  std::string operatorName = GetHLFullName(group, opcode, attribs);
   695	  std::string mangledName = operatorName + "." + name.str();
   696	  raw_string_ostream mangledNameStr(mangledName);
   697	  funcTy->print(mangledNameStr);
   698	  mangledNameStr.flush();
   699	
   700	  Function *F =
   701	      cast<Function>(M.getOrInsertFunction(mangledName, funcTy, attribs));
   702	
   703	  F->setLinkage(llvm::GlobalValue::LinkageTypes::InternalLinkage);
   704	
   705	  return F;
   706	}

   709	                      unsigned Opcode, Type *RetTy, ArrayRef<Value *> Args,
   710	                      IRBuilder<> &Builder) {
   711	  AttributeSet attribs;

   713	                        Builder);
   714	}
   715	
   716	Value *callHLFunction(Module &Module, HLOpcodeGroup OpcodeGroup,
   717	                      unsigned Opcode, Type *RetTy, ArrayRef<Value *> Args,
   718	                      const AttributeSet &attribs, IRBuilder<> &Builder) {
   719	  SmallVector<Type *, 4> ArgTys;
   720	  ArgTys.reserve(Args.size());
   721	  for (Value *Arg : Args)
   722	    ArgTys.emplace_back(Arg->getType());
   723	
   724	  FunctionType *FuncTy = FunctionType::get(RetTy, ArgTys, /* isVarArg */ false);
   725	  Function *Func =
   726	      GetOrCreateHLFunction(Module, FuncTy, OpcodeGroup, Opcode, attribs);
   727	
   728	  return Builder.CreateCall(Func, Args);
   729	}

Interesting! There's a type mismatch. The `DstN` calculation is wrong. Let me check:

`DstN<F8_E4M3FN, F16, 16>::Value = (16 * ComponentTypeTraits<F16>::ElementsPerScalar) / ComponentTypeTraits<F8_E4M3FN>::ElementsPerScalar`

For `F16`: `ElementsPerScalar = 1`
For `F8_E4M3FN`: `ElementsPerScalar = 4`

So `DstN = (16 * 1) / 4 = 4`

But the error says `DstN<...>::Value aka 16`. That means `ElementsPerScalar` for `F8_E4M3FN` is returning 1 instead of 4!

Let me check the `ComponentTypeTraits` specialization for `F8_E4M3FN`:

Looking at the header:
```cpp
template <ComponentEnum CompTy> struct ComponentTypeTraits {
  using Type = uint;
  static const bool IsNativeScalar = false;
  static const uint ElementsPerScalar = 4;
};

#define __MATRIX_SCALAR_COMPONENT_MAPPING(enum_val, type)                      \
  template <> struct ComponentTypeTraits<enum_val> {                           \
    using Type = type;                                                         \
    static const bool IsNativeScalar = true;                                   \
    static const uint ElementsPerScalar = 1;                                   \
  };
```

The default template has `ElementsPerScalar = 4` (for 8-bit types). But `F8_E4M3FN` is not listed in the `__MATRIX_SCALAR_COMPONENT_MAPPING` macros - only I16, U16, F16, I32, U32, F32, I64, U64, F64 are listed. So `F8_E4M3FN` should use the default template with `ElementsPerScalar = 4`.

But wait, the error says `Value aka 16`. Let me look at the error more carefully:


Good, so the F8_E4M3FN type does work in some contexts. Now let me look more at the actual PR issue. The PR description says there's an incorrect shufflevector. Let me look at the specific DXIL output pattern:

```
%6 = shufflevector <16 x half> %5, <16 x half> undef, <4 x i32> <i32 0, i32 1, i32 2, i32 3>
%7 = call <4 x i32> @dx.op.linAlgConvert.v4i32.v4f16(i32 -2147483618, <4 x half> %6, i32 8, i32 21)
```

The shuffle takes the first 4 elements of a `<16 x half>` and then calls `linAlgConvert` with `<4 x half>`. But the convert should take all 16 elements.

Now let me understand where this shuffle comes from. Looking at the `TranslateLinAlgConvert` function:

```cpp
Value *TranslateLinAlgConvert(CallInst *CI, IntrinsicOp IOP, OP::OpCode OpCode,
                              HLOperationLowerHelper &Helper,
                              HLObjectOperationLowerHelper *ObjHelper,
                              bool &Translated) {
  hlsl::OP *HlslOp = &Helper.hlslOP;
  IRBuilder<> Builder(CI);

  Value *OutVecPtr = CI->getArgOperand(1);
  Type *OutVecTy = OutVecPtr->getType()->getPointerElementType();
  Value *InVec = CI->getArgOperand(2);
  Value *InInterp = CI->getArgOperand(3);
  Value *OutInterp = CI->getArgOperand(4);

  Constant *OpArg = HlslOp->GetU32Const((unsigned)OpCode);
  Function *DxilFunc = HlslOp->GetOpFunc(OpCode, {OutVecTy, InVec->getType()});

  Value *OutVec =
      Builder.CreateCall(DxilFunc, {OpArg, InVec, InInterp, OutInterp});
  Builder.CreateStore(OutVec, OutVecPtr);

  return nullptr;
}
```

This function takes `InVec` directly from the call instruction argument and passes it to the DXIL function. So the shuffle must be happening BEFORE this lowering pass.

The shuffle must be generated during clang codegen. Let me look at how the Convert function call is generated. The Convert function creates a `Result` vector and calls `__builtin_LinAlg_Convert(Result, Vec, OriginTy, DestTy)`. 

The issue is likely that the `Result` type is `vector<uint, 4>` but the clang codegen is generating a call with mismatched vector sizes. Let me trace through the clang codegen for the intrinsic call.

Let me look at how the intrinsic function type is resolved when the arguments have different vector sizes. The intrinsic table has both `ret` and `vec` as `LITEMPLATE_ANY`. The `ret` is `vector<uint, 4>` and `vec` is `vector<half, 16>`. 

But wait - the intrinsic function type must have matching types for the template parameters? Or can they be different?

Let me look at how the intrinsic function type is constructed. The intrinsic has:
- Arg 1 (ret): `uTemplateId = 1`, `uLegalTemplates = LITEMPLATE_ANY`
- Arg 2 (vec): `uTemplateId = 2`, `uLegalTemplates = LITEMPLATE_ANY`

Each has its own template slot, so they can be different types! That should work.

But then where does the shuffle come from? Let me search for where shufflevector might be introduced for vector arguments of different sizes.

That's just for splatting, not relevant.

Let me think about this differently. The PR description shows that when converting from `<16 x half>` to fp8, the dxil shows:

```
%6 = shufflevector <16 x half> %5, <16 x half> undef, <4 x i32> <i32 0, i32 1, i32 2, i32 3>
%7 = call <4 x i32> @dx.op.linAlgConvert.v4i32.v4f16(i32 -2147483618, <4 x half> %6, i32 8, i32 21)
```

The function is `v4i32.v4f16` which means the result is `<4 x i32>` and input is `<4 x f16>`. But the input should be `<16 x f16>` and the result should be `<4 x i32>` (since 16 fp16 values = 4 packed fp8 values).

So the expected function should be `v4i32.v16f16` - result `<4 x i32>`, input `<16 x f16>`. 

The problem seems to be that the clang codegen is generating a function with signature `v4i32.v4f16` instead of `v4i32.v16f16`, and to compensate, it shuffles the `<16 x half>` down to `<4 x half>`.

This suggests that somewhere, the input vector type is being incorrectly matched to the output vector type. Let me look at the code in `EmitHLSLBuiltinCallExpr` or related functions that handle the intrinsic call.

So:
- `IA_SPECIAL_BASE = 0xf0` (240)
- `IA_SPECIAL_SLOTS = 4`
- `IA_R = 0xf0` (special ID = 0)
- `IA_C = 0xf1` (special ID = 1)
- `IA_R2 = 0xf2` (special ID = 2)
- `IA_C2 = 0xf3` (special ID = 3)

The logic at lines 7086-7092:
```cpp
if (pIntrinsicArg->uRows >= IA_SPECIAL_BASE) {
    UINT uSpecialId = pIntrinsicArg->uRows - IA_SPECIAL_BASE;
    if (uSpecialSize[uSpecialId] > TypeInfoRows) {
        uSpecialSize[uSpecialId] = TypeInfoRows;
    }
}
```

This takes the **minimum** of all rows that share the same special ID. Similarly for columns.

So if both `ret` and `vec` use `IA_R` for rows and `IA_C` for columns, then:
- `uSpecialSize[0]` (for IA_R) = min(rows of ret, rows of vec) = min(1, 1) = 1
- `uSpecialSize[1]` (for IA_C) = min(cols of ret, cols of vec) = min(4, 16) = 4

Then later, when the actual function type is built, these sizes are used for ALL arguments that reference these special IDs. So `vec` would get 4 columns instead of 16!

This is the bug! The `IA_R` and `IA_C` are meant to match sizes across arguments that should have the same dimensions (like matrix operations where the dimensions must match). But for `LinAlgConvert`, the input and output vectors can legitimately have different sizes.

The fix should be to use different special IDs for `ret` and `vec` so they don't interfere with each other. Looking at the available special IDs: `IA_R` (0), `IA_C` (1), `IA_R2` (2), `IA_C2` (3). 

For `LinAlgConvert`, the `ret` and `vec` should use different special slots. E.g., `ret` could use `IA_R`/`IA_C` and `vec` could use `IA_R2`/`IA_C2`.

The intrinsic table for `__builtin_LinAlg_Convert`:
```cpp

{"vec", AR_QUAL_IN, 2, LITEMPLATE_ANY, 2, LICOMPTYPE_NUMERIC, IA_R, IA_C},
```

Both use `IA_R` and `IA_C`. They should use different ones.

But actually, let me think about this more carefully. The `IA_R` and `IA_C` are meant to say "this argument's rows/columns should match the function's template rows/columns". When multiple arguments share the same special ID, they are forced to have the same size.

For `LinAlgConvert`, the input and output vectors have different sizes because the element types have different `ElementsPerScalar`. The `ret` type is `vector<uint, 4>` and `vec` type is `vector<half, 16>`. They should NOT share the same row/column constraints.

And earlier, `uSpecialSize[0]` was set to `min(rows of all args with IA_R)` and `uSpecialSize[1]` was set to `min(cols of all args with IA_C)`.

So for `LinAlgConvert`:
- `ret` uses `IA_R`/`IA_C` → gets rows from `uSpecialSize[0]`, cols from `uSpecialSize[1]`
- `vec` uses `IA_R`/`IA_C` → gets rows from `uSpecialSize[0]`, cols from `uSpecialSize[1]`

Both get the same sizes! And the sizes are the minimum of the two arguments' sizes.

The fix should be to change the intrinsic table so that `ret` and `vec` use DIFFERENT special size slots. We can change `vec` to use `IA_R2`/`IA_C2` instead of `IA_R`/`IA_C`.

```cpp
static const BYTE IA_R = 0xf0;
static const BYTE IA_C = 0xf1;
static const BYTE IA_R2 = 0xf2;
static const BYTE IA_C2 = 0xf3;
```

And `IA_SPECIAL_SLOTS = 4`. So there are 4 special slots: `IA_R`, `IA_C`, `IA_R2`, `IA_C2`.

For `LinAlgConvert`, we need the `ret` and `vec` to have independent sizes. So we should use:
- `ret`: `IA_R` / `IA_C` (slots 0, 1)
- `vec`: `IA_R2` / `IA_C2` (slots 2, 3)

    10	//
    11	// Intrinsic declarations are a line of the form:

    13	//   <type> \[\[[attr]\]\] <name>([<qual> <type> <name> [, ... ]]) [ : <op>]
    14	//
    15	// <name> is a C++ identifier for the intrinsic or argument name.
    16	//

    23	// variadic functions assume <qual> of "in" for any arguments that are not
    24	// explicitly specified.

    30	// or it can require an N-vector with "bool<N>" or an N-by-M

    34	// the size comes from the parse input.  "<>" means any kind

```
void [[min_sm=6.10]] __builtin_LinAlg_Convert(out numeric<> ret, in numeric<> vec, in uint input_interp, in uint output_interp);
```

Both `ret` and `vec` use `numeric<>`. The `<>` means any layout. The issue is that when this gets translated to the intrinsic table, both `ret` and `vec` get `IA_R` and `IA_C` for their rows and columns, which share the same special slots.

Let me look at how the gen_intrin_main.txt is processed. The `<>` after `numeric` means the layout is unconstrained. But the generated table uses `IA_R`/`IA_C` for both.

Let me check the generation script to understand this better:

    60	def format_comment(prefix, val):
    61	    "Formats a value with a line-comment prefix."
    62	    result = ""
    63	    line_width = 80
    64	    content_width = line_width - len(prefix)
    65	    l = len(val)
    66	    while l:
    67	        if l < content_width:
    68	            result += prefix + val.strip()
    69	            result += "\n"
    70	            l = 0
    71	        else:
    72	            split_idx = val.rfind(" ", 0, content_width)
    73	            result += prefix + val[:split_idx].strip()
    74	            result += "\n"
    75	            val = val[split_idx + 1 :]
    76	            l = len(val)
    77	    return result

2026-05-28 15:22:28,851 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I see the critical part! At lines 9612-9617:

```python
def do_any(m):
    base_type = m.group(1)
    rows = "r"
    cols = "c"
    template_list = "LITEMPLATE_ANY"
    return base_type, rows, cols, template_list
```

When the type is `numeric<>` (matched by `type_any_re`), it sets `rows = "r"` and `cols = "c"`. These get translated via `translate_rowcol` to `IA_R` and `IA_C`.

So EVERY argument that uses `<>` gets `IA_R` and `IA_C` for its rows and columns! This means all such arguments share the same size slots.

For most intrinsics, this is correct - you want the output and input to have matching sizes. But for `LinAlgConvert`, the input and output vectors can have DIFFERENT sizes because the element types have different `ElementsPerScalar` values.

The fix should be to change the definition of `__builtin_LinAlg_Convert` to use different row/col references for `ret` and `vec`. Looking at the available row/col references:
- `r`, `c` - primary rows/columns
- `r2`, `c2` - secondary rows/columns

So we could change the intrinsic definition from:
```
void __builtin_LinAlg_Convert(out numeric<> ret, in numeric<> vec, in uint input_interp, in uint output_interp);
```
to:
```
void __builtin_LinAlg_Convert(out numeric<r, c> ret, in numeric<r2, c2> vec, in uint input_interp, in uint output_interp);
```

This way, `ret` uses `r`/`c` (IA_R/IA_C) and `vec` uses `r2`/`c2` (IA_R2/IA_C2), which are independent slots. Each would track its own size.

But wait, I need to verify that this change is correct and won't break other things. Let me first check if there are other places where `IA_R2`/`IA_C2` are used to understand the pattern.

Let me check the gen_intrin_main.txt for examples of `r2`/`c2` usage
